Little Nemo entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror.

Little Nemo entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps.

###Scheherazade's Story About Jorge Luis Borges

There was once a cybertextual data structure just on the other side of the garden wall. Jorge Luis Borges couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Jorge Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. And that was where the encounter between a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and a member of royalty named Asterion took place. Jorge Luis Borges offered advice to Asterion in the form of a story. So Jorge Luis Borges began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." 

And he told the following story:

####Jorge Luis Borges's Story About Kublai Khan

There was once a recursive house of many doors that was also this story as I tell it to you. Kublai Khan must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way.

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, dominated by a koi pond with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. At the darkest hour Kublai Khan found the exit.

#Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a queen of Persia named Scheherazade, a king of Persia named Shahryar and an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer. Scheherazade suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


##Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan, a queen of Persia named Scheherazade and a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo. Kublai Khan suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Kublai Khan told:

###Kublai Khan's Story About Murasaki Shikibu

There was once a mysterious labyrinth from which few emerged. Murasaki Shikibu must have gotten lost, because she was wandering there. Murasaki Shikibu chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a wide and low fogou, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Murasaki Shikibu felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. And that was where the encounter between a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu and a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges took place. Jorge Luis Borges offered advice to Murasaki Shikibu in the form of a story. So Jorge Luis Borges began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Jorge Luis Borges told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Jorge Luis Borges said, ending the story. 

Murasaki Shikibu decided to travel onwards. Murasaki Shikibu opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead.

###Kublai Khan's Story About Little Nemo

There was once a cybertextual data structure that was a map of itself. Little Nemo was lost, like so many before and after, and he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way.

###Kublai Khan's Story About Jorge Luis Borges

Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror.

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Scheherazade wandered, lost in thought. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Scheherazade chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Scheherazade wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Scheherazade chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror.

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Scheherazade muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened.

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Scheherazade muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Scheherazade entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Scheherazade entered a rough fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. At the darkest hour Scheherazade found the exit.

Thus Kublai Khan ended his 2nd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

This is the story that Kublai Khan told:

##Kublai Khan's Story About Little Nemo

There was once a cybertextual data structure that was a map of itself. Little Nemo was lost, like so many before and after, and he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Little Nemo entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Little Nemo entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Little Nemo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Little Nemo entered a rough peristyle, dominated by a koi pond framed by a pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a lararium with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Little Nemo entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Little Nemo entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Little Nemo entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Little Nemo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Little Nemo entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Little Nemo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. Almost unable to believe it, Little Nemo discovered the way out.

##Kublai Khan's Story About Jorge Luis Borges

There was once a cybertextual data structure just on the other side of the garden wall. Jorge Luis Borges couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Jorge Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. And that was where the encounter between a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and a member of royalty named Asterion took place. Jorge Luis Borges offered advice to Asterion in the form of a story. So Jorge Luis Borges began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." 

And he told the following story:

###Jorge Luis Borges's Story About Kublai Khan

There was once a recursive house of many doors that was also this story as I tell it to you. Kublai Khan must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow liwan, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, tastefully offset by moki steps. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by moki steps with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough terrace, tastefully offset by moki steps. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow liwan, dominated by a lararium framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. At the darkest hour Kublai Khan found the exit.

#Scheherazade's Story About Murasaki Shikibu

There was once a mysterious labyrinth from which few emerged. Murasaki Shikibu must have gotten lost, because she was wandering there. Murasaki Shikibu chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Murasaki Shikibu felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. And that was where the encounter between a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu and a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges took place. Jorge Luis Borges offered advice to Murasaki Shikibu in the form of a story. So Jorge Luis Borges began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Jorge Luis Borges told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Jorge Luis Borges said, ending the story. 

Murasaki Shikibu decided to travel onwards. Murasaki Shikibu opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Murasaki Shikibu felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by divans lining the perimeter with a design of acanthus. Murasaki Shikibu felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Murasaki Shikibu walked away from that place. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a rough fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Murasaki Shikibu muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Murasaki Shikibu thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Murasaki Shikibu wandered, lost in thought. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Murasaki Shikibu felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror.

#Scheherazade's Story About Scheherazade

There was once an expansive zone that had never known the light of the sun. Scheherazade couldn't quite say how she was wandering there. Scheherazade wandered, lost in thought. 

Scheherazade entered a terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Scheherazade opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Scheherazade entered a wide and low fogou, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Scheherazade entered a peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade walked away from that place. 

Scheherazade entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Scheherazade muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way.

#Scheherazade's Story About Jorge Luis Borges

There was once a cybertextual data structure just on the other side of the garden wall. Jorge Luis Borges couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Jorge Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. And that was where the encounter between a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and a member of royalty named Asterion took place. Jorge Luis Borges offered advice to Asterion in the form of a story. So Jorge Luis Borges began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." 

And he told the following story:

##Jorge Luis Borges's Story About Kublai Khan

There was once a recursive house of many doors that was also this story as I tell it to you. Kublai Khan must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, dominated by a koi pond with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a fogou, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Kublai Khan entered a fogou, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. At the darkest hour Kublai Khan found the exit.

"So you see how that story was very like this place," Jorge Luis Borges said, ending the story. 

Jorge Luis Borges decided to travel onwards. Jorge Luis Borges wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Jorge Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a terrace, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Jorge Luis Borges felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorge Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a rough fogou, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Jorge Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Jorge Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Jorge Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Jorge Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Jorge Luis Borges muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened.

Jorge Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorge Luis Borges felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Jorge Luis Borges walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Jorge Luis Borges chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a high terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Jorge Luis Borges discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Jorge Luis Borges entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Jorge Luis Borges thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. At the darkest hour Jorge Luis Borges found the exit.

##Geoffery Chaucer's Story About Dunyazad

There was once a recursive house of many doors that contained the entire world. Dunyazad must have spoken the unutterable word, because she had arrived in that place. Dunyazad muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened.

Dunyazad entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dunyazad discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence.

#Scheherazade's Story About Shahryar

There was once an architectural forest that was also this story as I tell it to you. Shahryar must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out.

Shahryar entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Shahryar wandered, lost in thought. 

Shahryar entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Shahryar entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low fogou, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps.

Shahryar entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar walked away from that place.

##Virgil's Story About Virgil

There was once a twisted garden that contained the entire world. Virgil must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Virgil wandered, lost in thought. 

Virgil entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Virgil entered a liwan, tastefully offset by moki steps. Virgil felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Virgil entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Virgil chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Virgil entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Virgil muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Virgil entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Virgil felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Virgil entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Virgil wandered, lost in thought. 

Virgil entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Virgil walked away from that place. 

Virgil entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by moki steps with a design of acanthus. Virgil felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Virgil entered a cramped and narrow terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Virgil thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Virgil entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by moki steps. Virgil chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Virgil entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Virgil thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Virgil entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Virgil thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Virgil entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Virgil entered a cramped and narrow kiva, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Virgil entered a rough kiva, dominated by a moasic with a design of acanthus. Virgil thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Virgil entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. And that was where the encounter between a poet of Rome named Virgil and a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges took place. Jorge Luis Borges offered advice to Virgil in the form of a story. So Jorge Luis Borges began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." 

And he told the following story:

###Jorge Luis Borges's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges, a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan and an explorer of Venice named Marco Polo. Marco Polo suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Marco Polo told a very exciting story. Thus Marco Polo ended his 1st story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Marco Polo told:

####Marco Polo's Story About Asterion

There was once a twilight dimention in space that was also this story as I tell it to you. Asterion couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Asterion wandered, lost in thought. 

Asterion entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Asterion felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Asterion entered a wide and low peristyle, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Asterion chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Asterion entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Asterion muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Asterion entered a luxurious tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Asterion opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Asterion entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Asterion felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Asterion entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Asterion walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Asterion entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Asterion wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Asterion entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Asterion felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Asterion entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Asterion wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Asterion entered a rough kiva, dominated by a fallen column with a design of arabseque. Asterion muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Asterion entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Asterion discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Asterion entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Asterion muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Asterion entered a luxurious tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Asterion felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Asterion entered a high fogou, dominated by a fallen column which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. There was a book here, and he opened it and read the following page:

#Scheherazade's Story About Scheherazade

Scheherazade entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Scheherazade walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Scheherazade entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Scheherazade chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Scheherazade entered a high fogou, dominated by a koi pond which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Scheherazade felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Scheherazade entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of arabseque. Scheherazade thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Scheherazade entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Scheherazade felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. Almost unable to believe it, Scheherazade found the exit. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 58th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

#Scheherazade's Story About Dante Alighieri

There was once a library that was a map of itself. Dante Alighieri didn't know why he happened to be there. Dante Alighieri opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a moasic. Dante Alighieri opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. At the darkest hour Dante Alighieri discovered the way out.

#Scheherazade's Story About Virgil

There was once an expansive zone that was a map of itself. Virgil must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Virgil felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Virgil entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Virgil thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Virgil entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Virgil entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Virgil opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead.

Virgil entered a kiva, tastefully offset by moki steps. Virgil walked away from that place. 

Virgil entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil wandered, lost in thought. 

Virgil entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Virgil walked away from that place. 

Virgil entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Virgil walked away from that place. 

Virgil entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Virgil muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Virgil entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Virgil walked away from that place. 

Virgil entered a kiva, tastefully offset by moki steps. Virgil walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Virgil entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Virgil opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Virgil entered a peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Virgil walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way.

##Homer's Story

Once upon a time, there was the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad, a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo and a blind poet named Homer. Homer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Homer told:


###Homer's Story

Once upon a time, there was a king of Persia named Shahryar, a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu and an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer. Shahryar suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Shahryar told:

####Shahryar's Story About Dunyazad

There was once a twilight dimention in space that lived in eternal twilight. Dunyazad was almost certain about why she happened to be there. Dunyazad walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of acanthus. Dunyazad wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of acanthus. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dunyazad wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dunyazad muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Dunyazad discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Dunyazad entered a liwan, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dunyazad muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of acanthus. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a high terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. There was a book here, and she opened it and read the following page:

#Scheherazade's Story About Dunyazad

There was once an expansive zone, a place where many had become lost. Dunyazad was almost certain about why she happened to be there. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Dunyazad entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Dunyazad walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Dunyazad entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Dunyazad walked away from that place. 

Dunyazad entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dunyazad entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Dunyazad thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Dunyazad entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Dunyazad discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Dunyazad chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Dunyazad entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Dunyazad felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dunyazad entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Dunyazad felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Dunyazad entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Dunyazad opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Dunyazad entered a high terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dunyazad wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. Quite unexpectedly Dunyazad discovered the way out. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 68th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

#Scheherazade's Story About Homer

There was once a twisted garden that contained the entire world. Homer must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Homer entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Homer entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Homer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Homer entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. There was a book here, and he opened it and read the following page:

"Well," he said, "It is as confusing as this maze. Maybe it's in a language I don't know."

Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Homer entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Homer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a moasic. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Homer entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. There was a book here, and he opened it and read the following page:

"Well," he said, "Maybe it's a clue to where the exit is."

Homer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Homer entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Homer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Homer entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Homer walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Homer entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Homer walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Homer entered a high peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Homer walked away from that place. 

Homer entered a rough fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Homer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Homer entered a high tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Homer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Homer entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Homer wandered, lost in thought. Quite unexpectedly Homer reached the end of the labyrinth.

Thus Scheherazade ended her 69th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

#Scheherazade's Story About Kublai Khan

There was once a twisted garden from which few emerged. Kublai Khan wasn't quite sure where this was, only that he had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a moasic. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Kublai Khan entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. There was a book here, and he opened it and read the following page:

Thus Scheherazade ended her 70th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

#Scheherazade's Story About Murasaki Shikibu

There was once a twisted garden that contained the entire world. Murasaki Shikibu wasn't quite sure where this was, only that she had come to that place, as we all eventually must. Murasaki Shikibu felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Murasaki Shikibu muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Murasaki Shikibu walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Murasaki Shikibu walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Murasaki Shikibu walked away from that place. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Murasaki Shikibu discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Murasaki Shikibu muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Murasaki Shikibu wandered, lost in thought. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of acanthus. Murasaki Shikibu felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Murasaki Shikibu muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of acanthus. Murasaki Shikibu thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a high terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Murasaki Shikibu felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a high terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Murasaki Shikibu muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Murasaki Shikibu discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. There was a book here, and she opened it and read the following page:

#Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan, a queen of Persia named Scheherazade and a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu. Kublai Khan suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Kublai Khan told:

##Kublai Khan's Story About Geoffery Chaucer

Geoffery Chaucer entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way.

#Scheherazade's Story About Geoffery Chaucer

There was once an engmatic labyrinth that was a map of itself. Geoffery Chaucer had followed a secret path, and so he had arrived in that place. Geoffery Chaucer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Geoffery Chaucer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Geoffery Chaucer felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Geoffery Chaucer muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Geoffery Chaucer discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Geoffery Chaucer entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. There was a book here, and he opened it and read the following page:

#Scheherazade's Story About Marco Polo

There was once a mysterious labyrinth from which few emerged. Marco Polo couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Marco Polo walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious fogou, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Marco Polo walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Marco Polo walked away from that place. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a rough liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of arabseque. Marco Polo walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Marco Polo entered a rough fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. Almost unable to believe it, Marco Polo reached the end of the labyrinth.

#Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu, a member of royalty named Asterion and a queen of Persia named Scheherazade. Scheherazade suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

##Scheherazade's Story About Murasaki Shikibu

There was once a cybertextual data structure, a place where many had become lost. Murasaki Shikibu couldn't quite say how she was wandering there. Murasaki Shikibu muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Murasaki Shikibu muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Murasaki Shikibu thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Murasaki Shikibu chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Murasaki Shikibu opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Murasaki Shikibu entered a rough fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. There was a book here, and she opened it and read the following page:

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


#Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a king of Persia named Shahryar, a member of royalty named Asterion and the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad. Shahryar suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Shahryar told:


##Shahryar's Story

Once upon a time, there was a queen of Persia named Scheherazade, a philosopher named Socrates and a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges. Scheherazade suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

###Scheherazade's Story About Shahryar

There was once a twilight dimention in space that was also this story as I tell it to you. Shahryar was almost certain about why he happened to be there. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Shahryar opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Shahryar entered a high terrace, dominated by a koi pond which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Shahryar entered a high terrace, dominated by a koi pond which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Shahryar entered a liwan, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Shahryar entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a koi pond framed by a pattern of arabseque. Shahryar walked away from that place. 

Shahryar entered a luxurious liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Shahryar walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Shahryar opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Shahryar walked away from that place. 

Shahryar entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Shahryar thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Shahryar entered a high fogou, dominated by moki steps which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Shahryar walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a luxurious liwan, dominated by a sipapu framed by a pattern of acanthus. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Shahryar entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Shahryar entered a rough liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Shahryar felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Shahryar entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Shahryar discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Shahryar entered a high kiva, dominated by a lararium with a design of acanthus. Shahryar wandered, lost in thought. 

Shahryar entered a high kiva, dominated by a lararium with a design of acanthus. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Shahryar entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a fireplace with a design of arabseque. Shahryar chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Shahryar entered a terrace, dominated by a fountain which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Shahryar entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Shahryar muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Shahryar entered a terrace, dominated by moki steps which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Shahryar felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Shahryar entered a terrace, dominated by moki steps which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Shahryar opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. Almost unable to believe it, Shahryar found the exit. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 1st story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


###Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu, a king of Persia named Shahryar and an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer. Geoffery Chaucer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Geoffery Chaucer told:


####Geoffery Chaucer's Story

Once upon a time, there was an explorer of Venice named Marco Polo, a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer. Marco Polo suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Marco Polo told:

#####Marco Polo's Story About Marco Polo

There was once an engmatic labyrinth that was a map of itself. Marco Polo must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Marco Polo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious kiva, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Marco Polo wandered, lost in thought. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious kiva, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Marco Polo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Marco Polo entered a high kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Marco Polo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Marco Polo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. Almost unable to believe it, Marco Polo found the exit. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Marco Polo said, ending his story. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Geoffery Chaucer said, ending his story. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 2nd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


###Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a philosopher named Socrates, a blind poet named Homer and a queen of Persia named Scheherazade. Scheherazade suggested that she should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

####Scheherazade's Story About Marco Polo

There was once an engmatic labyrinth that was a map of itself. Marco Polo must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Marco Polo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Marco Polo entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Marco Polo wandered, lost in thought. 

Marco Polo entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by divans lining the perimeter framed by a pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. Quite unexpectedly Marco Polo found the exit. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Scheherazade said, ending her story. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 3rd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


###Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a king of Persia named Shahryar and a member of royalty named Asterion. Homer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Homer told:

####Homer's Story About Kublai Khan

There was once a library with many forking paths. Kublai Khan must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a high fogou, dominated by moki steps which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow kiva, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. And that was where the encounter between a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan and a king of Persia named Shahryar took place. Shahryar offered advice to Kublai Khan in the form of a story. So Shahryar began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." 

And he told the following story:

#####Shahryar's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a king of Persia named Shahryar. Dante Alighieri suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. Thus Dante Alighieri ended his 1st story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:


######Dante Alighieri's Story

Once upon a time, there was a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo, a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad. Jorge Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Jorge Luis Borges told:

#######Jorge Luis Borges's Story About Little Nemo

There was once an architectural forest, which is the world. Little Nemo must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a cramped and narrow fogou, dominated by a sipapu which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. Which was where Little Nemo reached the end of the labyrinth. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Jorge Luis Borges said, ending his story. 

---

Thus Dante Alighieri ended his 2nd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:

######Dante Alighieri's Story About Dante Alighieri

There was once a library that was a map of itself. Dante Alighieri couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri wandered, lost in thought. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a fogou, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. And there Dante Alighieri reached the end of the labyrinth. 

---

Thus Dante Alighieri ended his 3rd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Dante Alighieri said, ending his story.

"So you see how that story was very like this place," Shahryar said, ending the story.

Kublai Khan entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way.

Kublai Khan entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Kublai Khan chose an exit at random and walked that way. At the darkest hour Kublai Khan reached the end of the labyrinth.

"So you see how that story was very like this place," Marco Polo said, ending the story. 

Marco Polo decided to travel onwards. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way. At the darkest hour Marco Polo reached the end of the labyrinth. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Scheherazade said, ending her story. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 3rd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Thus Scheherazade ended her 4th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


##Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a king of Persia named Shahryar and a member of royalty named Asterion. Homer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Homer told:

###Homer's Story About Kublai Khan

There was once a library with many forking paths. Kublai Khan must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a luxurious liwan, dominated by a fountain framed by a pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a rough liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. And that was where the encounter between a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan and a king of Persia named Shahryar took place. Shahryar offered advice to Kublai Khan in the form of a story. So Shahryar began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." 

And he told the following story:

####Shahryar's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a king of Persia named Shahryar. Dante Alighieri suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. Thus Dante Alighieri ended his 1st story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:


#####Dante Alighieri's Story

Once upon a time, there was a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo, a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad. Jorge Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Jorge Luis Borges told:

######Jorge Luis Borges's Story About Little Nemo

There was once an architectural forest, which is the world. Little Nemo must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a high terrace, tastefully offset by a fountain. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a high liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low peristyle, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. And that was where the encounter between a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo and a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri took place. Little Nemo offered advice to Dante Alighieri in the form of a story. So Little Nemo began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Little Nemo told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Little Nemo said, ending the story. 

Little Nemo decided to travel onwards. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious fogou, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Little Nemo entered a cramped and narrow kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. There was a book here, and he opened it and read the following page:

Little Nemo walked away from that place. 

Little Nemo entered a peristyle, dominated by a lararium framed by a pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence.

#####Dante Alighieri's Story About Dante Alighieri

There was once a library that was a map of itself. Dante Alighieri couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high fogou, dominated by moki steps which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri wandered, lost in thought. 

Dante Alighieri entered a luxurious fogou, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a koi pond framed by a pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a cramped and narrow kiva, dominated by a sipapu with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. And there Dante Alighieri reached the end of the labyrinth.

#Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a lady of the Imperial Court named Murasaki Shikibu, a king of Persia named Shahryar and an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer. Geoffery Chaucer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Geoffery Chaucer told:


##Geoffery Chaucer's Story

Once upon a time, there was an explorer of Venice named Marco Polo, a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and an English poet named Geoffery Chaucer. Marco Polo suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Marco Polo told:

###Marco Polo's Story About Marco Polo

There was once an engmatic labyrinth that was a map of itself. Marco Polo must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Marco Polo wandered, lost in thought. 

Marco Polo entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Marco Polo entered a rough kiva, dominated by a fallen column with a design of arabseque. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Marco Polo entered a rough kiva, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Marco Polo entered a cramped and narrow fogou, dominated by moki steps which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Marco Polo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, dominated by a lararium framed by a pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, dominated by a lararium framed by a pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo walked away from that place. 

Marco Polo entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. And that was where the encounter between an explorer of Venice named Marco Polo and a king of Persia named Shahryar took place. Marco Polo offered advice to Shahryar in the form of a story. So Marco Polo began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Marco Polo told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Marco Polo said, ending the story. 

Marco Polo decided to travel onwards. Marco Polo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way. 

Marco Polo entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Marco Polo felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. Quite unexpectedly Marco Polo discovered the way out. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Marco Polo said, ending his story. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Geoffery Chaucer said, ending his story. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 80th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..."
