Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. And that was where the encounter between a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan and a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges took place. Kublai Khan offered advice to Jorge Luis Borges in the form of a story. So Kublai Khan began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Kublai Khan told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Kublai Khan said, ending the story. 

Kublai Khan decided to travel onwards. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. Almost unable to believe it, Kublai Khan discovered the way out. 

---

"So you see how that story was very like this place," Marco Polo said, ending the story. 

Marco Polo decided to travel onwards. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Marco Polo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened. 

Marco Polo entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Marco Polo felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Marco Polo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Marco Polo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Marco Polo entered a luxurious terrace, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Marco Polo muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Marco Polo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Marco Polo discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Marco Polo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Marco Polo wandered, lost in thought, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. Quite unexpectedly Marco Polo discovered the way out. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Scheherazade said, ending her story. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 81st story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Thus Scheherazade ended her 82nd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


#Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a king of Persia named Shahryar and a member of royalty named Asterion. Homer suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Homer told:

##Homer's Story About Kublai Khan

There was once a library with many forking paths. Kublai Khan must have gotten lost, because he was wandering there. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Kublai Khan muttered, "North, this way is probably north!" as the door opened, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of acanthus. Kublai Khan walked away from that place. 

Kublai Khan entered a cramped and narrow kiva, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Kublai Khan felt a bit dizzy at the confusion of doors. 

Kublai Khan entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. And that was where the encounter between a Khagan of the Ikh Mongol Uls named Kublai Khan and a king of Persia named Shahryar took place. Shahryar offered advice to Kublai Khan in the form of a story. So Shahryar began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." 

And he told the following story:

###Shahryar's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a king of Persia named Shahryar. Dante Alighieri suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. Thus Dante Alighieri ended his 1st story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:


####Dante Alighieri's Story

Once upon a time, there was a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo, a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad. Jorge Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Jorge Luis Borges told:

#####Jorge Luis Borges's Story About Little Nemo

There was once an architectural forest, which is the world. Little Nemo must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a moasic. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a rough peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a rough peristyle, tastefully offset by moki steps. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. And that was where the encounter between a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo and a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri took place. Little Nemo offered advice to Dante Alighieri in the form of a story. So Little Nemo began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Little Nemo told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Little Nemo said, ending the story. 

Little Nemo decided to travel onwards. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a high liwan, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a terrace, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a peristyle, dominated by a fireplace framed by a pattern of acanthus. There was a book here, and he opened it and read the following page:

####Dante Alighieri's Story About Dante Alighieri

There was once a library that was a map of itself. Dante Alighieri couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dante Alighieri entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dante Alighieri wandered, lost in thought. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a rough peristyle, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. And there Dante Alighieri reached the end of the labyrinth.

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:

###Dante Alighieri's Story About Dante Alighieri

There was once a library that was a map of itself. Dante Alighieri couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Dante Alighieri wandered, lost in thought. 

Dante Alighieri entered a terrace, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high terrace, dominated by a moasic which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a cramped and narrow tetrasoon, tastefully offset by moki steps. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. And there Dante Alighieri reached the end of the labyrinth. 

---

Thus Dante Alighieri ended his 3rd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Dante Alighieri said, ending his story.

"So you see how that story was very like this place," Shahryar said, ending the story. 

Kublai Khan decided to travel onwards. Kublai Khan wandered, lost in thought. 

Kublai Khan entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Kublai Khan opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Kublai Khan entered a liwan, tastefully offset by a fountain. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Kublai Khan discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else. 

Kublai Khan entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, not knowing that it was indeed the wrong way. 

Kublai Khan entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Kublai Khan walked away from that place, listening to the echo of footsteps. Quite unexpectedly Kublai Khan reached the end of the labyrinth.

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


#Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind poet named Homer, a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri and a king of Persia named Shahryar. Dante Alighieri suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. Thus Dante Alighieri ended his 1st story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Dante Alighieri told:


##Dante Alighieri's Story

Once upon a time, there was a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo, a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges and the sister of Scheherazade named Dunyazad. Jorge Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Jorge Luis Borges told:

###Jorge Luis Borges's Story About Little Nemo

There was once an architectural forest, which is the world. Little Nemo must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a high kiva, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco with a design of acanthus. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Little Nemo entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. And that was where the encounter between a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo and a poet exiled from Florence named Dante Alighieri took place. Little Nemo offered advice to Dante Alighieri in the form of a story. So Little Nemo began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Little Nemo told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Little Nemo said, ending the story. 

Little Nemo decided to travel onwards. Little Nemo wandered, lost in thought. 

Little Nemo entered a wide and low peristyle, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious fogou, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Little Nemo thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Little Nemo entered a liwan, dominated by a trompe-l'oeil fresco framed by a pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious peristyle, dominated by a koi pond framed by a pattern of arabseque. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Little Nemo entered a luxurious peristyle, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Little Nemo opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Little Nemo entered a kiva, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. There was a book here, and he opened it and read the following page:

##Dante Alighieri's Story About Dante Alighieri

There was once a library that was a map of itself. Dante Alighieri couldn't quite say how he was wandering there. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high terrace, dominated by a koi pond which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri wandered, lost in thought. 

Dante Alighieri entered a fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a cramped and narrow liwan, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high kiva, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dante Alighieri entered a peristyle, tastefully offset by divans lining the perimeter. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Dante Alighieri entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a high liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. 

Dante Alighieri entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Dante Alighieri wandered, lost in thought. 

Dante Alighieri entered a luxurious fogou, dominated by divans lining the perimeter which was lined with a repeated pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Dante Alighieri entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Dante Alighieri thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a fogou, dominated by a fireplace which was lined with a repeated pattern of arabseque. Dante Alighieri felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low liwan, dominated by an obelisk framed by a pattern of acanthus. Dante Alighieri opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by moki steps with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead.

"Well," he said, "Perhaps it's a list of names? Or a crossword puzzle that was filled in wrong."

Dante Alighieri walked away from that place. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low liwan, tastefully offset by a fireplace. Dante Alighieri discovered that one of the doors lead somewhere else, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Dante Alighieri entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of acanthus. Dante Alighieri chose an exit at random and walked that way, listening to the echo of footsteps. At the darkest hour Dante Alighieri found the exit. 

---

Thus Dante Alighieri ended his 3rd story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Dante Alighieri told a very exciting story. "And that was how it happened," Dante Alighieri said, ending his story. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 86th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." And Scheherazade told a very exciting story. Thus Scheherazade ended her 87th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:


#Scheherazade's Story

Once upon a time, there was a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges, a child trying to go to Slumberland named Little Nemo and a queen of Persia named Scheherazade. Jorge Luis Borges suggested that he should tell a story, because it was Alex's birthday. So he began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Jorge Luis Borges told:

##Jorge Luis Borges's Story About Homer

There was once a mysterious labyrinth that lived in eternal twilight. Homer must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Homer entered a high liwan, dominated by a fallen column framed by a pattern of arabseque. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a cramped and narrow peristyle, dominated by moki steps framed by a pattern of acanthus. Homer wandered, lost in thought. 

Homer entered a kiva, dominated by an obelisk with a design of arabseque. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Homer entered a luxurious tetrasoon, dominated by a sipapu with a design of arabseque. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a luxurious peristyle, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Homer entered a tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. And that was where the encounter between a blind poet named Homer and a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges took place. Homer offered advice to Jorge Luis Borges in the form of a story. So Homer began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Homer told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Homer said, ending the story. 

Homer decided to travel onwards. Homer wandered, lost in thought. 

Homer entered a kiva, dominated by a koi pond with a design of arabseque. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Homer entered a rough kiva, tastefully offset by a trompe-l'oeil fresco. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Homer entered a high peristyle, tastefully offset by a moasic. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Homer entered a high peristyle, dominated by a moasic framed by a pattern of acanthus. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. Which was where Homer discovered the way out. 

---

"And that was how it happened," Jorge Luis Borges said, ending his story. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 88th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."

So she began, "It is related, O august king, that..." 

This is the story that Scheherazade told:

#Scheherazade's Story About Homer

There was once a mysterious labyrinth that lived in eternal twilight. Homer must have spoken the unutterable word, because he had arrived in that place. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Homer entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a kiva, dominated by moki steps with a design of arabseque. Homer wandered, lost in thought. 

Homer entered a rough tetrasoon, tastefully offset by a fallen column. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead. 

Homer entered a wide and low peristyle, tastefully offset by a koi pond. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out. 

Homer entered a fogou, tastefully offset by a fountain. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Homer entered a kiva, tastefully offset by an obelisk. And that was where the encounter between a blind poet named Homer and a blind librarian named Jorge Luis Borges took place. Homer offered advice to Jorge Luis Borges in the form of a story. So Homer began, "It seems to me that this place we find ourselves reminds me of when..." And Homer told a very exciting story. "So you see how that story was very like this place," Homer said, ending the story. 

Homer decided to travel onwards. Homer wandered, lost in thought. 

Homer entered a wide and low tetrasoon, dominated by a fountain with a design of arabseque. Homer chose an exit at random and walked that way. 

Homer entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Homer thought that this direction looked promising, and went that way, humming a little to relieve the silence. 

Homer entered a wide and low terrace, tastefully offset by a sipapu. Homer felt sure that this must be the way out, sparing a passing glance at a mirror. 

Homer entered a kiva, tastefully offset by a fountain. Homer opened a door, not feeling quite sure where it lead, passing a reflection in a mirror. Which was where Homer discovered the way out. 

---

Thus Scheherazade ended her 89th story, saying, "But there is another tale which is more marvelous still."
